      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Equatorial_Guinea_Map.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Equatorial_Guinea_Map.png/300px-Equatorial_Guinea_Map.png" decoding="async" width="300" height="372" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Equatorial_Guinea_Map.png/450px-Equatorial_Guinea_Map.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Equatorial_Guinea_Map.png/600px-Equatorial_Guinea_Map.png 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="1240"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Equatorial_Guinea_Map.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>
         <div class="center" style="width:auto; margin-left:auto; margin-right:auto;">
          Equatorial Guinea
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The current president of Equatorial Guinea is Teodoro Obiang. The 1982 constitution of Equatorial Guinea gives him extensive powers, including naming and dismissing members of the cabinet, making laws by decree, dissolving the Chamber of Representatives, negotiating and ratifying treaties and serving as commander in chief of the armed forces. Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Pascual_Obama_Asue" title="Francisco Pascual Obama Asue">Francisco Pascual Obama Asue</a> was appointed by Obiang and operates under powers delegated by the President.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>During the four decades of his rule, Obiang has shown little tolerance for opposition. While the country is nominally a multiparty democracy, its elections have generally been considered a sham. According to <a href="/wiki/Human_Rights_Watch" title="Human Rights Watch">Human Rights Watch</a>, the dictatorship of President Obiang used an <a href="/wiki/Oil_boom" title="Oil boom">oil boom</a> to entrench and enrich itself further at the expense of the country's people.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc.co.uk_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc.co.uk-61">[59]</a></sup> Since August 1979 some 12 real and perceived unsuccessful coup attempts have occurred.<sup id="cite_ref-HRW_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HRW-62">[60]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>According to a March 2004 BBC profile,<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[61]</a></sup> politics within the country were dominated by tensions between Obiang's son, <a href="/wiki/Teodoro_Nguema_Obiang_Mangue" title="Teodoro Nguema Obiang Mangue">Teodoro Nguema Obiang Mangue</a>, and other close relatives with powerful positions in the security forces. The tension may be rooted in a power shift arising from the dramatic increase in oil production which has occurred since 1997.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>In 2004 a plane load of suspected mercenaries was intercepted in <a href="/wiki/Zimbabwe" title="Zimbabwe">Zimbabwe</a> while allegedly on the way to overthrow Obiang. A November 2004 report<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[62]</a></sup> named <a href="/wiki/Mark_Thatcher" title="Mark Thatcher">Mark Thatcher</a> as a financial backer of the <a href="/wiki/2004_Equatorial_Guinea_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat_attempt" title="2004 Equatorial Guinea coup d'état attempt">2004 Equatorial Guinea coup d'état attempt</a> organized by <a href="/wiki/Simon_Mann" title="Simon Mann">Simon Mann</a>. Various accounts also named the United Kingdom's <a href="/wiki/Secret_Intelligence_Service" title="Secret Intelligence Service">MI6</a>, the United States' <a href="/wiki/Central_Intelligence_Agency" title="Central Intelligence Agency">CIA</a>, and Spain as tacit supporters of the coup attempt.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[63]</a></sup> Nevertheless, the <a href="/wiki/Amnesty_International" title="Amnesty International">Amnesty International</a> report released in June 2005<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[64]</a></sup> on the ensuing trial of those allegedly involved highlighted the prosecution's failure to produce conclusive evidence that a coup attempt had actually taken place. Simon Mann was released from prison on 3 November 2009 for humanitarian reasons.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[65]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Since 2005, <a href="/wiki/Military_Professional_Resources_Inc." title="Military Professional Resources Inc.">Military Professional Resources Inc.</a>, a US-based international private military company, has worked in Equatorial Guinea to train police forces in appropriate human rights practices. In 2006, <a href="/wiki/United_States_Secretary_of_State" title="United States Secretary of State">US Secretary of State</a> <a href="/wiki/Condoleezza_Rice" title="Condoleezza Rice">Condoleezza Rice</a> hailed Obiang as a "good friend" despite repeated criticism of his human rights and civil liberties record. The <a href="/wiki/US_Agency_for_International_Development" class="mw-redirect" title="US Agency for International Development">US Agency for International Development</a> entered into a memorandum of understanding (MOU) with Obiang, in April 2006, to establish a social development Fund in the country, implementing projects in the areas of health, education, women's affairs and the environment.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[66]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2006, Obiang signed an anti-torture decree banning all forms of abuse and improper treatment in Equatorial Guinea, and commissioned the renovation and modernization of Black Beach prison in 2007 to ensure the humane treatment of prisoners.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[67]</a></sup> However, human rights abuses have continued. Human Rights Watch and Amnesty International among other non-governmental organizations have documented severe human rights abuses in prisons, including torture, beatings, unexplained deaths and illegal detention.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[68]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[69]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The anti-corruption lobby <a href="/wiki/Transparency_International" title="Transparency International">Transparency International</a> put Equatorial Guinea in the top 12 of its list of most corrupt states. Freedom House, a pro-democracy and human rights NGO, described Obiang as one of the world's "most kleptocratic living autocrats," and complained about the US government welcoming his administration and buying oil from it.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[70]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Obiang was re-elected to serve an additional term in 2009 in <a href="/wiki/Equatorial_Guinean_presidential_election,_2009" class="mw-redirect" title="Equatorial Guinean presidential election, 2009">an election</a> the <a href="/wiki/African_Union" title="African Union">African Union</a> deemed "in line with electoral law".<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[71]</a></sup> Obiang re-appointed Prime Minister Ignacio Milam Tang in 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[72]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:177px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Teodoro_Obiang_detail,_1650FRP051.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Teodoro_Obiang_detail%2C_1650FRP051.jpg/175px-Teodoro_Obiang_detail%2C_1650FRP051.jpg" decoding="async" width="175" height="230" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Teodoro_Obiang_detail%2C_1650FRP051.jpg/263px-Teodoro_Obiang_detail%2C_1650FRP051.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Teodoro_Obiang_detail%2C_1650FRP051.jpg/350px-Teodoro_Obiang_detail%2C_1650FRP051.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1026" data-file-height="1351"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Teodoro_Obiang_detail,_1650FRP051.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>According to the BBC, President <a href="/wiki/Teodoro_Obiang_Nguema_Mbasogo" title="Teodoro Obiang Nguema Mbasogo">Obiang Nguema</a> "has been described by rights organisations as one of Africa's most brutal dictators."<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[73]</a></sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In November 2011, a new constitution was approved. The vote on the constitution was taken though neither the text or its content was revealed to the public before the vote. Under the new constitution the president was limited to a maximum of two seven-year terms and would be both the head of state and head of the government, therefore eliminating the prime minister. The new constitution also introduced the figure of a vice president and called for the creation of a 70-member senate with 55 senators elected by the people and the 15 remaining designated by the president. Surprisingly, in the following cabinet reshuffle it was announced that there would be two vice-presidents in clear violation of the constitution that was just taking effect.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[74]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In October 2012, during an interview with <a href="/wiki/Christiane_Amanpour" title="Christiane Amanpour">Christiane Amanpour</a> on <a href="/wiki/CNN" title="CNN">CNN</a>, Obiang was asked whether he would step down at the end of the current term (2009–2016) since the new constitution limited the number of terms to two and he has been reelected at least 4 times. Obiang answered he refused to step aside because the new constitution was not retroactive and the two- term limit would only become applicable from 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[75]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>26 May 2013 elections combined the senate, lower house and mayoral contests all in a single package. Like all previous elections, this was denounced by the opposition and it too was won by Obiang's PDGE. During the electoral contest, the ruling party hosted internal elections which were later scrapped as none of the president's favorite candidates led the internal lists. Ultimately, the ruling party and the satellites of the ruling coalition decided to run not based on the candidates but based on the party. This created a situation where during the election the ruling party's coalition did not provide the names of their candidates so effectively individuals were not running for office, instead the party was the one running for office.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>The May 2013 elections were marked by a series of events including the popular protest planned by a group of activists from the MPP (Movement of Popular Protest) which included several social and political groups. The MPP called for a peaceful protest at the Plaza de la Mujer square on 15 May. MPP coordinator Enrique Nsolo Nzo was arrested and official state media portrayed him as planning to destabilize the country and depose the president. However, and despite speaking under duress and with clear signs of torture, Nsolo said that they had planned a peaceful protest and had indeed obtained all the legal authorizations required to carry out the peaceful protest. In addition to that, he firmly stated that he was not affiliated with any political party. The Plaza de la Mujer square in Malabo was occupied by the police from 13 May and it has been heavily guarded ever since. The government embarked on a <a href="/wiki/Censorship" title="Censorship">censorship</a> program that affected social sites including Facebook and other websites that were critical to the government of Equatorial Guinea. The censorship was implemented by redirecting online searches to the official government website.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>Shortly after the elections, opposition party CPDS announced that they were going to protest peacefully against the 26 May elections on 25 June.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[76]</a></sup> Interior minister Clemente Engonga refused to authorize the protest on the grounds that it could "destabilize" the country and CPDS decided to go forward, claiming constitutional right. On the night of 24 June, the CPDS headquarters in Malabo were surrounded by heavily armed police officers to keep those inside from leaving and thus effectively blocking the protest. Several leading members of CPDS were detained in Malabo and others in Bata were kept from boarding several local flights to Malabo.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Armed_Forces">Armed Forces</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Equatorial_Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Armed Forces">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Armed_Forces_of_Equatorial_Guinea" title="Armed Forces of Equatorial Guinea">Armed Forces of Equatorial Guinea</a> consists of approximately 2,500 service members.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[77]</a></sup> The army has almost 1,400 soldiers, the police 400 paramilitary men, the navy 200 service members, and the air force about 120 members. There is also a gendarmerie, but the number of members is unknown. The Gendarmerie is a new branch of the service in which training and education is being supported by the French Military Cooperation in Equatorial Guinea.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Equatorial_Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Equatorial_Guinea" title="Geography of Equatorial Guinea">Geography of Equatorial Guinea</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Equatorial Guinea is on the west coast of <a href="/wiki/Central_Africa" title="Central Africa">Central Africa</a>. The country consists of a mainland territory, <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Muni" title="Río Muni">Río Muni</a>, which is bordered by Cameroon to the north and Gabon to the east and south, and five small islands, <a href="/wiki/Bioko" title="Bioko">Bioko</a>, <a href="/wiki/Corisco" title="Corisco">Corisco</a>, <a href="/wiki/Annob%C3%B3n" title="Annobón">Annobón</a>, <a href="/wiki/Elobey_Chico" title="Elobey Chico">Elobey Chico</a> (Small Elobey), and <a href="/wiki/Elobey_Grande" title="Elobey Grande">Elobey Grande</a> (Great Elobey). Bioko, the site of the capital, <a href="/wiki/Malabo" title="Malabo">Malabo</a>, lies about 40 kilometers (25&nbsp;mi) off the coast of Cameroon. Annobón Island is about 350 kilometers (220&nbsp;mi) west-south-west of <a href="/wiki/Cape_Lopez" title="Cape Lopez">Cape Lopez</a> in Gabon. Corisco and the two Elobey islands are in Corisco Bay, on the border of Río Muni and Gabon. </p>
      <p>Equatorial Guinea lies between latitudes <a href="/wiki/4th_parallel_north" title="4th parallel north">4°N</a> and <a href="/wiki/2nd_parallel_south" title="2nd parallel south">2°S</a>, and longitudes <a href="/wiki/5th_meridian_west" title="5th meridian west">5°</a> and <a href="/wiki/12th_meridian_east" title="12th meridian east">12°E</a>. Despite its name, no part of the country's territory lies on the equator—it is in the northern hemisphere, except for the insular <a href="/wiki/Annob%C3%B3n_Province" class="mw-redirect" title="Annobón Province">Annobón Province</a>, which is about 155&nbsp;km (96&nbsp;mi) south of the equator. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Equatorial_Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Koppen-Geiger_Map_GNQ_present.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Koppen-Geiger_Map_GNQ_present.svg/220px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_GNQ_present.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="135" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Koppen-Geiger_Map_GNQ_present.svg/330px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_GNQ_present.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Koppen-Geiger_Map_GNQ_present.svg/440px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_GNQ_present.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1386" data-file-height="850"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Koppen-Geiger_Map_GNQ_present.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Köppen climate classification of Equatorial Guinea
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Equatorial Guinea has a tropical climate with distinct wet and dry seasons. From June to August, Río Muni is dry and Bioko wet; from December to February, the reverse occurs. In between there is gradual transition. Rain or mist occurs daily on Annobón, where a cloudless day has never been registered. The temperature at Malabo, Bioko, ranges from 16&nbsp;°C (61&nbsp;°F) to 33&nbsp;°C (91&nbsp;°F), though on the southern <a href="/w/index.php?title=Moka_Plateau&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Moka Plateau (page does not exist)">Moka Plateau</a> normal high temperatures are only 21&nbsp;°C (70&nbsp;°F). In Río Muni, the average temperature is about 27&nbsp;°C (81&nbsp;°F). Annual <a href="/wiki/Rainfall" class="mw-redirect" title="Rainfall">rainfall</a> varies from 1,930&nbsp;mm (76&nbsp;in) at Malabo to 10,920&nbsp;mm (430&nbsp;in) at <a href="/wiki/San_Antonio_de_Ureca" title="San Antonio de Ureca">Ureka</a>, Bioko, but Río Muni is somewhat drier.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[78]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ecology">Ecology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Equatorial_Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Ecology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Equatorial Guinea spans several <a href="/wiki/Ecoregion" title="Ecoregion">ecoregions</a>. Río Muni region lies within the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Equatorial_coastal_forests" title="Atlantic Equatorial coastal forests">Atlantic Equatorial coastal forests</a> ecoregion except for patches of <a href="/wiki/Central_African_mangroves" title="Central African mangroves">Central African mangroves</a> on the coast, especially in the <a href="/wiki/Muni_River" title="Muni River">Muni River</a> estuary. The <a href="/wiki/Cross-Sanaga-Bioko_coastal_forests" title="Cross-Sanaga-Bioko coastal forests">Cross-Sanaga-Bioko coastal forests</a> ecoregion covers most of Bioko and the adjacent portions of <a href="/wiki/Cameroon" title="Cameroon">Cameroon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">Nigeria</a> on the African mainland, and the <a href="/wiki/Mount_Cameroon_and_Bioko_montane_forests" title="Mount Cameroon and Bioko montane forests">Mount Cameroon and Bioko montane forests</a> ecoregion covers the highlands of Bioko and nearby <a href="/wiki/Mount_Cameroon" title="Mount Cameroon">Mount Cameroon</a>. The <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Tom%C3%A9,_Pr%C3%ADncipe,_and_Annob%C3%B3n_moist_lowland_forests" class="mw-redirect" title="São Tomé, Príncipe, and Annobón moist lowland forests">São Tomé, Príncipe, and Annobón moist lowland forests</a> ecoregion covers all of Annobón, as well as São Tomé and Príncipe.<sup id="cite_ref-DinersteinOlson2017_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DinersteinOlson2017-81">[79]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The country had a 2018 <a href="/wiki/Forest_Landscape_Integrity_Index" title="Forest Landscape Integrity Index">Forest Landscape Integrity Index</a> mean score of 7.99/10, ranking it 30<sup>th</sup> globally out of 172 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-FLII-Supplementary_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FLII-Supplementary-82">[80]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Equatorial_Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Subdivisions_of_Equatorial_Guinea" title="Subdivisions of Equatorial Guinea">Subdivisions of Equatorial Guinea</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="floatright">
       <div class="noresize" style="height: 334px; width: 350px; ">
        <map name="ImageMap_4091b79419034c16"><area href="/wiki/Annob%C3%B3n_Province" shape="rect" coords="3,35,11,47" alt="Annobón Province" title="Annobón Province"><area href="/wiki/Bioko_Norte_Province" shape="rect" coords="10,2,19,11" alt="Bioko Norte Province" title="Bioko Norte Province"><area href="/wiki/Bioko_Sur_Province" shape="rect" coords="5,13,14,23" alt="Bioko Sur Province" title="Bioko Sur Province"><area href="/wiki/Centro_Sur_Province" shape="rect" coords="51,25,60,36" alt="Centro Sur Province" title="Centro Sur Province"><area href="/wiki/Ki%C3%A9-Ntem_Province" shape="rect" coords="81,8,90,19" alt="Kié-Ntem Province" title="Kié-Ntem Province"><area href="/wiki/Litoral_Province_(Equatorial_Guinea)" shape="rect" coords="29,24,38,36" alt="Litoral Province (Equatorial Guinea)" title="Litoral Province (Equatorial Guinea)"><area href="/wiki/Wele-Nzas_Province" shape="rect" coords="78,30,88,42" alt="Wele-Nzas Province" title="Wele-Nzas Province"></map>
        <img alt="A clickable map of Equatorial Guinea exhibiting its two regions and seven provinces." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Equatorial_Guinea%2C_administrative_divisions_-_de_-_colored_2020.svg/350px-Equatorial_Guinea%2C_administrative_divisions_-_de_-_colored_2020.svg.png" decoding="async" width="350" height="334" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Equatorial_Guinea%2C_administrative_divisions_-_de_-_colored_2020.svg/525px-Equatorial_Guinea%2C_administrative_divisions_-_de_-_colored_2020.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Equatorial_Guinea%2C_administrative_divisions_-_de_-_colored_2020.svg/700px-Equatorial_Guinea%2C_administrative_divisions_-_de_-_colored_2020.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1091" data-file-height="1042" usemap="#ImageMap_4091b79419034c16">
        <div style="margin-left: 0px; margin-top: -20px; text-align: left;">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Equatorial_Guinea,_administrative_divisions_-_de_-_colored_2020.svg" title="About this image"><img alt="About this image" src="/w/extensions/ImageMap/resources/desc-20.png?15600" style="border: none;"></a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Equatorial Guinea is divided into eight <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_Equatorial_Guinea" title="Provinces of Equatorial Guinea">provinces</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-statoids_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-statoids-83">[81]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[82]</a></sup> The newest province is <a href="/wiki/Djibloho" title="Djibloho">Djibloho</a>, created in 2017 with its headquarters at <a href="/wiki/Ciudad_de_la_Paz" title="Ciudad de la Paz">Ciudad de la Paz</a>, the country's future capital.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[83]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[84]</a></sup> The other seven provinces are as follows (numbers correspond to those on the map; provincial capitals appear in parentheses):<sup id="cite_ref-statoids_83-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-statoids-83">[81]</a></sup> </p> 
      <ol>
       <li><a href="/wiki/Annob%C3%B3n" title="Annobón">Annobón</a> (<a href="/wiki/San_Antonio_de_Pal%C3%A9" title="San Antonio de Palé">San Antonio de Palé</a>)</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Bioko_Norte" title="Bioko Norte">Bioko Norte</a> (<a href="/wiki/Malabo" title="Malabo">Malabo</a>)</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Bioko_Sur" title="Bioko Sur">Bioko Sur</a> (<a href="/wiki/Luba,_Equatorial_Guinea" title="Luba, Equatorial Guinea">Luba</a>)</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Centro_Sur" title="Centro Sur">Centro Sur</a> (<a href="/wiki/Evinayong" title="Evinayong">Evinayong</a>)</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Ki%C3%A9-Ntem" title="Kié-Ntem">Kié-Ntem</a> (<a href="/wiki/Ebebiy%C3%ADn" class="mw-redirect" title="Ebebiyín">Ebebiyín</a>)</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Litoral_(Equatorial_Guinea)" title="Litoral (Equatorial Guinea)">Litoral</a> (<a href="/wiki/Bata,_Equatorial_Guinea" title="Bata, Equatorial Guinea">Bata</a>)</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Wele-Nzas" title="Wele-Nzas">Wele-Nzas</a> (<a href="/wiki/Mongomo" title="Mongomo">Mongomo</a>)</li>
      </ol> 
      <p>The provinces are further divided into 19 districts and 37 <a href="/wiki/Municipalities_of_Equatorial_Guinea" title="Municipalities of Equatorial Guinea">municipalities</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[85]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Wildlife">Wildlife</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Equatorial_Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Wildlife">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Wildlife_of_Equatorial_Guinea" title="Wildlife of Equatorial Guinea">Wildlife of Equatorial Guinea</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Equatorial Guinea is home to <a href="/wiki/Gorilla" title="Gorilla">gorillas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chimpanzee" title="Chimpanzee">chimpanzees</a>, various monkeys, <a href="/wiki/Leopard" title="Leopard">leopards</a>, <a href="/wiki/African_Buffalo" class="mw-redirect" title="African Buffalo">buffalo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Antelope" title="Antelope">antelope</a>, <a href="/wiki/Elephant" title="Elephant">elephants</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hippopotamus" title="Hippopotamus">hippopotamuses</a>, <a href="/wiki/Crocodile" title="Crocodile">crocodiles</a>, and various <a href="/wiki/Snake" title="Snake">snakes</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Pythonidae" title="Pythonidae">pythons</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[86]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Equatorial_Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Equatorial_Guinea" title="Economy of Equatorial Guinea">Economy of Equatorial Guinea</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Gepetrol_HQ_Malabo_2013.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Gepetrol_HQ_Malabo_2013.jpg/220px-Gepetrol_HQ_Malabo_2013.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="259" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Gepetrol_HQ_Malabo_2013.jpg/330px-Gepetrol_HQ_Malabo_2013.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Gepetrol_HQ_Malabo_2013.jpg/440px-Gepetrol_HQ_Malabo_2013.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1605" data-file-height="1893"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Gepetrol_HQ_Malabo_2013.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Gepetrol Tower in Malabo 2013
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Before independence Equatorial Guinea exported <a href="/wiki/Cocoa_bean" title="Cocoa bean">cocoa</a>, coffee and timber, mostly to its colonial ruler, Spain, but also to Germany and the UK. On 1 January 1985, the country became the first non-<a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/Francophone" class="extiw" title="wikt:Francophone">Francophone</a> African member of the <a href="/wiki/Franc_zone" class="mw-redirect" title="Franc zone">franc zone</a>, adopting the <a href="/wiki/CFA_franc" title="CFA franc">CFA franc</a> as its currency. The national currency, the <a href="/wiki/Ekwele" class="mw-redirect" title="Ekwele">ekwele</a>, had previously been linked to the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_peseta" title="Spanish peseta">Spanish peseta</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-web.archive.org_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-web.archive.org-89">[87]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The discovery of large <a href="/wiki/Oil_reserves" title="Oil reserves">oil reserves</a> in 1996 and its subsequent exploitation contributed to a dramatic increase in government revenue. As of 2004<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Equatorial_Guinea&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>,<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[88]</a></sup> Equatorial Guinea is the third-largest oil producer in <a href="/wiki/Sub-Saharan_Africa" title="Sub-Saharan Africa">Sub-Saharan Africa</a>. Its oil production has risen to 360,000 barrels per day (57,000&nbsp;m<sup>3</sup>/d), up from 220,000 only two years earlier. </p>
      <p>Forestry, farming, and fishing are also major components of GDP. Subsistence farming predominates. The deterioration of the rural economy under successive brutal regimes has diminished any potential for agriculture-led growth. </p>
      <p>In July 2004, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Senate" title="United States Senate">United States Senate</a> published an investigation into <a href="/wiki/Riggs_Bank" title="Riggs Bank">Riggs Bank</a>, a Washington-based bank into which most of Equatorial Guinea's oil revenues were paid until recently, and which also banked for <a href="/wiki/Chile" title="Chile">Chile</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Augusto_Pinochet" title="Augusto Pinochet">Augusto Pinochet</a>. The Senate report showed at least $35 million siphoned off by Obiang, his family and regime senior officials. The president has denied any wrongdoing. Riggs Bank in February 2005 paid $9 million in restitution for Pinochet's banking, no restitution was made with regard to Equatorial Guinea.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[89]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>From 2000 to 2010, Equatorial Guinea had the highest average annual increase in GDP (Gross Domestic Product), 17%.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[90]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Equatorial Guinea is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Organization_for_the_Harmonization_of_Business_Law_in_Africa" class="mw-redirect" title="Organization for the Harmonization of Business Law in Africa">Organization for the Harmonization of Business Law in Africa</a> (<a href="/wiki/OHADA" title="OHADA">OHADA</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-ohada.com_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ohada.com-93">[91]</a></sup> Equatorial Guinea tried to be validated as an <a href="/wiki/Extractive_Industries_Transparency_Initiative" title="Extractive Industries Transparency Initiative">Extractive Industries Transparency Initiative</a> (EITI)–compliant country, working toward transparency in reporting of oil revenues and prudent use of natural resource wealth. The country obtained candidate status on 22 February 2008. It was then required to meet a number of obligations to do so, including committing to working with civil society and companies on EITI implementation, appointing a senior individual to lead on EITI implementation, and publishing a fully costed Work Plan with measurable targets, a timetable for implementation and an assessment of capacity constraints. However, when Equatorial Guinea applied to extend the deadline for completing EITI validation, the EITI Board did not agree to the extension.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[92]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>According to the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a>, Equatorial Guinea has the highest GNI (Gross National Income) per capita of any African country, 83 times larger than the GNI per capita of <a href="/wiki/Burundi" title="Burundi">Burundi</a>, the poorest country.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[93]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Yet despite its impressive GNI figure, Equatorial Guinea is plagued by extreme poverty because its <a href="/wiki/Gini_coefficient" title="Gini coefficient">Gini coefficient</a> of 65.0 is the highest in the entire world. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">Transportation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Equatorial_Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Transportation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Equatorial_Guinea" title="Transport in Equatorial Guinea">Transport in Equatorial Guinea</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Due to the large oil industry in the country, internationally recognized carriers fly to <a href="/wiki/Malabo_International_Airport" title="Malabo International Airport">Malabo International Airport</a> which, in May 2014, had several direct connections to <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a> and <a href="/wiki/West_Africa" title="West Africa">West Africa</a>. There are three airports in Equatorial Guinea — <a href="/wiki/Malabo_International_Airport" title="Malabo International Airport">Malabo International Airport</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bata_Airport" title="Bata Airport">Bata Airport</a> and the new <a href="/wiki/Annobon_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Annobon Airport">Annobon Airport</a> on the island of <a href="/wiki/Annobon" class="mw-redirect" title="Annobon">Annobon</a>. <a href="/wiki/Malabo_International_Airport" title="Malabo International Airport">Malabo International Airport</a> is the only international airport. </p>
      <p>Every airline registered in Equatorial Guinea appears on the list of air carriers prohibited in the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> (EU) which means that they are banned from operating services of any kind within the EU.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[94]</a></sup> However freight carriers provide service from European cities to the capital. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Equatorial_Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Equatorial_Guinea" title="Demographics of Equatorial Guinea">Demographics of Equatorial Guinea</a>
      </div> 
      <div style="clear:both;"></div> 
      <table class="wikitable" style="float: right; margin-left: 10px"> 
       <caption>
        Population in Equatorial Guinea<sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP-97">[95]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_2019_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP_2019-98">[96]</a></sup> 
       </caption> 
       <tbody>
        <tr> 
         <th>Year </th> 
         <th>Million </th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td style="text-align:left;">1950</td> 
         <td style="text-align:right;">0.2 </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td style="text-align:left;">2000</td> 
         <td style="text-align:right;">0.6 </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td style="text-align:left;">2018</td> 
         <td style="text-align:right;">1.3 </td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Bubi_children.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Bubi_children.jpg/220px-Bubi_children.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="139" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/fa/Bubi_children.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="227" data-file-height="143"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Bubi_children.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Equatorial Guinean children of <a href="/wiki/Bubi_people" title="Bubi people">Bubi</a> descent
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The majority of the people of Equatorial Guinea are of <a href="/wiki/Bantu_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Bantu people">Bantu</a> origin.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[97]</a></sup> The largest ethnic group, the <a href="/wiki/Fang_people" title="Fang people">Fang</a>, is indigenous to the mainland, but substantial migration to <a href="/wiki/Bioko_Island" class="mw-redirect" title="Bioko Island">Bioko Island</a> since the 20th century means the Fang population exceeds that of the earlier <a href="/wiki/Bubi_people" title="Bubi people">Bubi</a> inhabitants. The Fang constitute 80% of the population<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[98]</a></sup> and comprise around 67 clans. Those in the northern part of <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Muni" title="Río Muni">Río Muni</a> speak Fang-Ntumu, while those in the south speak Fang-Okah; the two dialects have differences but are mutually intelligible. Dialects of Fang are also spoken in parts of neighboring Cameroon (Bulu) and Gabon. These dialects, while still intelligible, are more distinct. The <a href="/wiki/Bubi_people" title="Bubi people">Bubi</a>, who constitute 15% of the population, are indigenous to Bioko Island. The traditional demarcation line between Fang and 'Beach' (inland) ethnic groups was the village of <a href="/wiki/Niefang" title="Niefang">Niefang</a> (limit of the Fang), east of Bata. </p>
      <p>Coastal ethnic groups, sometimes referred to as <a href="/wiki/Ndowe" class="mw-redirect" title="Ndowe">Ndowe</a> or "Playeros" (<i>Beach People</i> in Spanish): <a href="/wiki/Combe_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Combe people">Combes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bujeba_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Bujeba people">Bujebas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Balengue_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Balengue people">Balengues</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Benga_people" title="Benga people">Bengas</a> on the mainland and small islands, and <a href="/wiki/Fernandinos" class="mw-redirect" title="Fernandinos">Fernandinos</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Leone_Krio_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Sierra Leone Krio people">Krio</a> community on Bioko Island together comprise 5% of the population. Europeans (largely of Spanish or <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_people" title="Portuguese people">Portuguese</a> descent, some with partial African ancestry) also live in the country, but most ethnic Spaniards left after independence. </p>
      <p>A growing number of foreigners from neighboring <a href="/wiki/Cameroon" title="Cameroon">Cameroon</a>, Nigeria, and <a href="/wiki/Gabon" title="Gabon">Gabon</a> have immigrated to the country. According to the <i>Encyclopedia of the Stateless Nations</i> (2002) 7% of Bioko islanders were <a href="/wiki/Igbo_people" title="Igbo people">Igbo</a>, an ethnic group from southeastern Nigeria.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[99]</a></sup> Equatorial Guinea received <a href="/wiki/Asians" class="mw-redirect" title="Asians">Asians</a> and native Africans from other countries as workers on cocoa and coffee plantations. Other black Africans came from <a href="/wiki/Liberia" title="Liberia">Liberia</a>, Angola, and <a href="/wiki/Mozambique" title="Mozambique">Mozambique</a>. Most of the Asian population is <a href="/wiki/Overseas_Chinese" title="Overseas Chinese">Chinese</a>, with small numbers of <a href="/wiki/Non-resident_Indian_and_person_of_Indian_origin" title="Non-resident Indian and person of Indian origin">Indians</a>. </p>
      <p>Equatorial Guinea has also been a destination for fortune-seeking European immigrants from Britain, France and Germany. Israelis and <a href="/wiki/Moroccan_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Moroccan people">Moroccans</a> also live and work here. <a href="/wiki/Petroleum" title="Petroleum">Oil extraction</a> since the 1990s has contributed to a doubling of the population in Malabo. After independence, thousands of Equatorial Guineans went to Spain. Another 100,000 Equatorial Guineans went to Cameroon, Gabon, and Nigeria because of the dictatorship of <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Mac%C3%ADas_Nguema" title="Francisco Macías Nguema">Francisco Macías Nguema</a>. Some Equatorial Guinean communities are also found in Latin America, the United States, Portugal, and France. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Equatorial_Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Malabo_(16511251451).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Malabo_%2816511251451%29.jpg/220px-Malabo_%2816511251451%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Malabo_%2816511251451%29.jpg/330px-Malabo_%2816511251451%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Malabo_%2816511251451%29.jpg/440px-Malabo_%2816511251451%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4928" data-file-height="3264"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Malabo_(16511251451).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Floral inscription with the name of the country in <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a> in <a href="/wiki/Malabo" title="Malabo">Malabo</a>, Equatorial Guinea
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>For years, the official languages were <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a> (the local variant is <a href="/wiki/Equatoguinean_Spanish" title="Equatoguinean Spanish">Equatoguinean Spanish</a>) and <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-5">[5]</a></sup> Portuguese was also adopted as an official language in 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-CPLP_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CPLP-102">[100]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-sol_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sol-103">[101]</a></sup> Spanish has been an official language since 1844. It is still the language of education and administration. 67.6% of Equatorial Guineans can speak it, especially those living in the capital, <a href="/wiki/Malabo" title="Malabo">Malabo</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-obi_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-obi-104">[102]</a></sup> French was only made official in order to join the <a href="/wiki/Organisation_internationale_de_la_Francophonie" title="Organisation internationale de la Francophonie">Francophonie</a> and it is not locally spoken, except in some border towns. </p>
      <p>Aboriginal languages are recognised as integral parts of the "national culture" (Constitutional Law No. 1/1998 21 January). Indigenous languages include <a href="/wiki/Fang_language" title="Fang language">Fang</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bube_language" title="Bube language">Bube</a>, <a href="/wiki/Benga_language" title="Benga language">Benga</a>, <a href="/wiki/Combe_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Combe language">Ndowe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Balengue_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Balengue language">Balengue</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bujeba_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Bujeba language">Bujeba</a>, Bissio, Gumu, Igbo, <a href="/wiki/Pichinglis" title="Pichinglis">Pichinglis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Annobonese_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Annobonese language">Fa d'Ambô</a> and the nearly extinct <a href="/wiki/Baseke_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Baseke language">Baseke</a>. Most African ethnic groups speak <a href="/wiki/Bantu_languages" title="Bantu languages">Bantu languages</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-GEpress_noticia134en_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GEpress_noticia134en-105">[103]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Santa_Isabel_Malabo_20131224_140204.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Santa_Isabel_Malabo_20131224_140204.jpg/300px-Santa_Isabel_Malabo_20131224_140204.jpg" decoding="async" width="300" height="400" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Santa_Isabel_Malabo_20131224_140204.jpg/450px-Santa_Isabel_Malabo_20131224_140204.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Santa_Isabel_Malabo_20131224_140204.jpg/600px-Santa_Isabel_Malabo_20131224_140204.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2448" data-file-height="3264"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Santa_Isabel_Malabo_20131224_140204.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Santa Isabel Cathedral in Malabo
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Annobonese_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Annobonese language">Fa d'Ambô</a>, a Portuguese creole, has vigorous use in <a href="/wiki/Annob%C3%B3n_Province" class="mw-redirect" title="Annobón Province">Annobón Province</a>, in Malabo (the capital), and among some speakers in Equatorial Guinea's mainland. Many residents of Bioko can also speak Spanish, particularly in the capital, and the local trade language <a href="/wiki/Pichinglis" title="Pichinglis">Pichinglis</a>, an English-based creole. Spanish is not spoken much in Annobón. In government and education Spanish is used. Noncreolized Portuguese is used as liturgical language by local Catholics.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[104]</a></sup> The Annobonese ethnic community tried to gain membership in the <a href="/wiki/Community_of_Portuguese_Language_Countries" title="Community of Portuguese Language Countries">Community of Portuguese Language Countries</a> (CPLP). The government financed an <a href="/wiki/International_Portuguese_Language_Institute" title="International Portuguese Language Institute">Instituto Internacional da Língua Portuguesa</a> (IILP) sociolinguistic study in Annobón. It documented strong links with the Portuguese creole populations in São Tomé and Príncipe, Cape Verde and Guinea-Bissau.<sup id="cite_ref-sol_103-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sol-103">[101]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Due to historical and cultural ties, in 2010 the legislature amended article four of the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Equatorial_Guinea" title="Constitution of Equatorial Guinea">Constitution of Equatorial Guinea</a>, to establish Portuguese as an official language of the Republic. This was an effort by the government to improve its communications, trade, and bilateral relations with Portuguese-speaking countries.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[105]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-GuineEqGov_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GuineEqGov-108">[106]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-GuineEqGovPDF_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GuineEqGovPDF-109">[107]</a></sup> It also recognises long historical ties with Portugal, and with Portuguese-speaking peoples of Brazil, São Tomé and Príncipe, and Cape Verde. </p>
      <p>Some of the motivations for Equatorial Guinea's membership pursuit into the <a href="/wiki/Community_of_Portuguese_Language_Countries" title="Community of Portuguese Language Countries">Community of Portuguese Language Countries</a> (CPLP) included access to several professional and academic exchange programmes and facilitated cross-border circulation of citizens.<sup id="cite_ref-obi_104-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-obi-104">[102]</a></sup> The adoption of Portuguese as an official language was the primary requirement to apply for CPLP acceptance. In addition, the country was told it must adopt political reforms allowing effective democracy and respect for human rights.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[108]</a></sup> The national parliament discussed this law in October 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-GEpress_noticia1980_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GEpress_noticia1980-111">[109]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In February 2012, Equatorial Guinea's foreign minister signed an agreement with the IILP on the promotion of Portuguese in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-IILP_Blog2012-02-07_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IILP_Blog2012-02-07-112">[110]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CPLP_News1875_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CPLP_News1875-113">[111]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In July 2012, the CPLP refused Equatorial Guinea full membership, primarily because of its continued serious violations of human rights. The government responded by legalising political parties, declaring a moratorium on the death penalty, and starting a dialog with all political factions.<sup id="cite_ref-sol_103-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sol-103">[101]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-expr_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-expr-114">[112]</a></sup> Additionally, the IILP secured land from the government for the construction of Portuguese language cultural centres in Bata and Malabo.<sup id="cite_ref-sol_103-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sol-103">[101]</a></sup> At its 10th summit in <a href="/wiki/Dili" title="Dili">Dili</a> in July 2014, Equatorial Guinea was admitted as a CPLP member. Abolition of the death penalty and the promotion of Portuguese as an official language were preconditions of the approval.<sup id="cite_ref-CPLP_NewsID1635_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CPLP_NewsID1635-115">[113]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Equatorial_Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="barbox tright" style="overflow-x: auto;"> 
       <div style="border:1px solid silver; font-size:88%; padding:0.4em; width:auto; background: white;"> 
        <table style="text-align:left; border-collapse:collapse; width:100%;">

           <td colspan="2" style="padding-left: 0.4em; padding-right: 0.4em; min-width: 8em;"><a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Equatorial_Guinea" title="Islam in Equatorial Guinea">Islam</a></td>

        </table> 
       </div> 
      </div> 
      <p>The principal religion in Equatorial Guinea is Christianity, the faith of 93% of the population. <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism_in_Equatorial_Guinea" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholicism in Equatorial Guinea">Roman Catholics</a> make up the majority (88%), while a minority are Protestants (5%). 2% of the population follows <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Equatorial_Guinea" title="Islam in Equatorial Guinea">Islam</a> (mainly <a href="/wiki/Sunni" class="mw-redirect" title="Sunni">Sunni</a>). The remaining 5% practise <a href="/wiki/Animism" title="Animism">Animism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%CA%BC%C3%AD_Faith_in_Equatorial_Guinea" title="Baháʼí Faith in Equatorial Guinea">Baháʼí</a>, and other beliefs.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[114]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Equatorial_Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Health_in_Equatorial_Guinea" title="Health in Equatorial Guinea">Health in Equatorial Guinea</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Equatorial Guinea's innovative <a href="/wiki/Malaria" title="Malaria">malaria</a> programs in the early 21st century achieved success in reducing <a href="/wiki/Malaria" title="Malaria">malaria</a> infection, disease, and <a href="/wiki/Mortality_rate" title="Mortality rate">mortality</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[115]</a></sup> Their program consists of twice-yearly indoor residual spraying (IRS), the introduction of artemisinin combination treatment (ACTs), the use of intermittent preventive treatment in pregnant women (IPTp), and the introduction of very high coverage with long-lasting insecticide-treated mosquito nets (LLINs). Their efforts resulted in a reduction in all-cause under-five mortality from 152 to 55 deaths per 1,000 live births (down 64%), a sharp drop that coincided with the launch of the program.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[116]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In June 2014 four cases of <a href="/wiki/Poliomyelitis" class="mw-redirect" title="Poliomyelitis">polio</a> were reported, the country's first outbreak of the disease.<sup id="cite_ref-EquatorialGuinea_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EquatorialGuinea-119">[117]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Equatorial_Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Equatorial_Guinea" title="Education in Equatorial Guinea">Education in Equatorial Guinea</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Ministerio_de_Educaci%C3%B3n,_Ciencia_y_Deportes_(Malabo)_(6510104101).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Ministerio_de_Educaci%C3%B3n%2C_Ciencia_y_Deportes_%28Malabo%29_%286510104101%29.jpg/300px-Ministerio_de_Educaci%C3%B3n%2C_Ciencia_y_Deportes_%28Malabo%29_%286510104101%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="300" height="200" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Ministerio_de_Educaci%C3%B3n%2C_Ciencia_y_Deportes_%28Malabo%29_%286510104101%29.jpg/450px-Ministerio_de_Educaci%C3%B3n%2C_Ciencia_y_Deportes_%28Malabo%29_%286510104101%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Ministerio_de_Educaci%C3%B3n%2C_Ciencia_y_Deportes_%28Malabo%29_%286510104101%29.jpg/600px-Ministerio_de_Educaci%C3%B3n%2C_Ciencia_y_Deportes_%28Malabo%29_%286510104101%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5184" data-file-height="3456"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Ministerio_de_Educaci%C3%B3n,_Ciencia_y_Deportes_(Malabo)_(6510104101).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Ministry of Education, Science and Sports (<i>Ministerio de Educación, Ciencia y Deportes</i>)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Under <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Macias" class="mw-redirect" title="Francisco Macias">Francisco Macias</a>, education was neglected, and few children received any type of education. Under President Obiang, the illiteracy rate dropped from 73% to 13%,<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_5-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-5">[5]</a></sup> and the number of primary school students rose from 65,000 in 1986 to more than 100,000 in 1994. Education is free and compulsory for children between the ages of 6 and 14.<sup id="cite_ref-web.archive.org_89-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-web.archive.org-89">[87]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Equatorial Guinea government has partnered with <a href="/wiki/Hess_Corporation" title="Hess Corporation">Hess Corporation</a> and The Academy for Educational Development (AED) to establish a $20 million education program for primary school teachers to teach modern child development techniques.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[118]</a></sup> There are now 51 model schools whose active pedagogy will be a national reform.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The date of the event predicted near this tag has passed. (December 2018)">needs update</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>In recent years,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (December 2018)">when?</span></a></i>]</sup> with change in the economic and political climate and government social agendas, several cultural dispersion and literacy organizations have been founded, chiefly with the financial support of the Spanish government. The country has one university, the <a href="/wiki/Universidad_Nacional_de_Guinea_Ecuatorial" class="mw-redirect" title="Universidad Nacional de Guinea Ecuatorial">Universidad Nacional de Guinea Ecuatorial</a> (UNGE), with a campus in Malabo and a Faculty of Medicine located in Bata on the mainland. In 2009 the university produced the first 110 national doctors. The Bata Medical School is supported principally by the government of Cuba and staffed by Cuban medical educators and physicians.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[119]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Equatorial_Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Equatorial_Guinea" title="Culture of Equatorial Guinea">Culture of Equatorial Guinea</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Malabo_a_13-oct-01.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Malabo_a_13-oct-01.jpg/220px-Malabo_a_13-oct-01.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Malabo_a_13-oct-01.jpg/330px-Malabo_a_13-oct-01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Malabo_a_13-oct-01.jpg/440px-Malabo_a_13-oct-01.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1792" data-file-height="1200"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Malabo_a_13-oct-01.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The port of <a href="/wiki/Malabo" title="Malabo">Malabo</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In June 1984, the First Hispanic-African Cultural Congress was convened to explore the cultural identity of Equatorial Guinea. The congress constituted the center of integration and the marriage of the Hispanic culture with African cultures.<sup id="cite_ref-web.archive.org_89-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-web.archive.org-89">[87]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Equatorial_Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Equatorial Guinea currently has no <a href="/wiki/UNESCO_World_Heritage_Site" class="mw-redirect" title="UNESCO World Heritage Site">UNESCO World Heritage Site</a> or tentative sites for the World Heritage List.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[120]</a></sup> The country also has no documented heritage listed in the <a href="/wiki/Memory_of_the_World_Programme" title="Memory of the World Programme">Memory of the World Programme</a> of UNESCO nor any intangible cultural heritage listed in the UNESCO <a href="/wiki/Intangible_Cultural_Heritage" class="mw-redirect" title="Intangible Cultural Heritage">Intangible Cultural Heritage</a> List.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[121]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[122]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Tourist attractions are the colonial quarter in Malabo, the southern part of the island Bioko where you can hike to the Iladyi cascades and to remote beaches to watch nesting turtles, Bata with its shoreline Paseo Maritimo and the tower of liberty, Mongomo with its <a href="/wiki/Basilica_of_the_Immaculate_Conception,_Mongomo" title="Basilica of the Immaculate Conception, Mongomo">basilica</a> (the second largest Catholic church in Africa) and the new planned and built capital <a href="/wiki/Ciudad_de_la_Paz" title="Ciudad de la Paz">Ciudad de la Paz</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media_and_communications">Media and communications</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Equatorial_Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Media and communications">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Media_in_Equatorial_Guinea" class="mw-redirect" title="Media in Equatorial Guinea">Media in Equatorial Guinea</a> and <a href="/wiki/Telecommunications_in_Equatorial_Guinea" title="Telecommunications in Equatorial Guinea">Telecommunications in Equatorial Guinea</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:UNED-GQ_IMG_6269_(6510136445).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/UNED-GQ_IMG_6269_%286510136445%29.jpg/300px-UNED-GQ_IMG_6269_%286510136445%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="300" height="200" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/UNED-GQ_IMG_6269_%286510136445%29.jpg/450px-UNED-GQ_IMG_6269_%286510136445%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/UNED-GQ_IMG_6269_%286510136445%29.jpg/600px-UNED-GQ_IMG_6269_%286510136445%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5184" data-file-height="3456"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:UNED-GQ_IMG_6269_(6510136445).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Edition of the television magazine "Malabeando" at the Cultural Center of Spain in Malabo.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The principal means of communication within Equatorial Guinea are 3 state-operated <a href="/wiki/FM_radio" class="mw-redirect" title="FM radio">FM radio</a> stations. <a href="/wiki/BBC_World_Service" title="BBC World Service">BBC World Service</a>, <a href="/wiki/Radio_France_Internationale" title="Radio France Internationale">Radio France Internationale</a> and Gabon-based Africa No 1 broadcast on FM in Malabo. There is also an independent radio called <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.radiomacuto.cl">Radio Macuto</a>, the voice of the voiceless. Radio Macuto is a web based radio a news source known for publishing news that call out Obiang's regime and call for the mobilization of the ecuatoguinean community to exercise freedom of speech and engage in politics. There are also five <a href="/wiki/Shortwave" class="mw-redirect" title="Shortwave">shortwave</a> radio stations. Television Nacional, the television network, is state operated.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_5-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-5">[5]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[123]</a></sup> The international TV programme RTVGE is available via satellites in Africa, Europa, and the Americas and worldwide via Internet.<sup id="cite_ref-Lyngsat_TVGE_126-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lyngsat_TVGE-126">[124]</a></sup> There are two newspapers and two magazines. </p>
      <p>Equatorial Guinea ranks at position 161 out of 179 countries in the 2012 <a href="/wiki/Reporters_Without_Borders" title="Reporters Without Borders">Reporters Without Borders</a> press freedom index. The watchdog says the national broadcaster obeys the orders of the information ministry. Most of the media companies practice <a href="/wiki/Self-censorship" title="Self-censorship">self-censorship</a>, and are banned by law from criticising public figures. The state-owned media and the main private radio station are under the directorship of the president's son, Teodor Obiang. </p>
      <p>Landline telephone penetration is low, with only two lines available for every 100 persons.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_5-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-5">[5]</a></sup> There is one <a href="/wiki/GSM" title="GSM">GSM</a> mobile telephone operator, with coverage of <a href="/wiki/Malabo" title="Malabo">Malabo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bata,_Equatorial_Guinea" title="Bata, Equatorial Guinea">Bata</a>, and several mainland cities.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[125]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[126]</a></sup> As of 2009<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Equatorial_Guinea&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, approximately 40% of the population subscribed to mobile telephone services.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_5-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-5">[5]</a></sup> The only telephone provider in Equatorial Guinea is Orange. </p>
      <p>There were more than 42,000 internet users by December 2011. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Equatorial_Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Equatorial_Guinea" title="Music of Equatorial Guinea">Music of Equatorial Guinea</a>
      </div> 
      <p>There is little <a href="/wiki/Popular_music" title="Popular music">popular music</a> coming out of Equatorial Guinea. Pan-African styles like <a href="/wiki/Soukous" title="Soukous">soukous</a> and <a href="/wiki/Makossa" title="Makossa">makossa</a> are popular, as are <a href="/wiki/Reggae" title="Reggae">reggae</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rock_and_roll" title="Rock and roll">rock and roll</a>. Acoustic guitar bands based on a Spanish model are the country's best-known indigenous popular tradition. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cinema">Cinema</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Equatorial_Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Cinema">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In 2014 the South African-Dutch-Equatorial Guinean drama film <a href="/wiki/Where_the_Road_Runs_Out" title="Where the Road Runs Out">Where the Road Runs Out</a> was shot in the country. There is also the documentary <i>The Writer From a Country Without Bookstores</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[127]</a></sup> that has still to be internationally premiered. It focuses in one of Equatorial Guinea's most translated writers <a href="/wiki/Juan_Tom%C3%A1s_%C3%81vila_Laurel" title="Juan Tomás Ávila Laurel">Juan Tomás Ávila Laurel</a>. It is the first feature film openly critical of Obiang's regime. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Equatorial_Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable selfref">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Category:Sport_in_Equatorial_Guinea" title="Category:Sport in Equatorial Guinea">Category:Sport in Equatorial Guinea</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Estadio_de_Bata_(15896733814).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Estadio_de_Bata_%2815896733814%29.jpg/220px-Estadio_de_Bata_%2815896733814%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Estadio_de_Bata_%2815896733814%29.jpg/330px-Estadio_de_Bata_%2815896733814%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Estadio_de_Bata_%2815896733814%29.jpg/440px-Estadio_de_Bata_%2815896733814%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Estadio_de_Bata_(15896733814).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Estadio_de_Bata" title="Estadio de Bata">Estadio de Bata</a> in <a href="/wiki/Bata,_Equatorial_Guinea" title="Bata, Equatorial Guinea">Bata</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Equatorial Guinea was chosen to co-host the <a href="/wiki/2012_African_Cup_of_Nations" class="mw-redirect" title="2012 African Cup of Nations">2012 African Cup of Nations</a> in partnership with <a href="/wiki/Gabon" title="Gabon">Gabon</a>, and hosted the <a href="/wiki/2015_Africa_Cup_of_Nations" title="2015 Africa Cup of Nations">2015 edition</a>. The country was also chosen to host the <a href="/wiki/2008_Women%27s_African_Football_Championship" class="mw-redirect" title="2008 Women's African Football Championship">2008 Women's African Football Championship</a>, which they won. The <a href="/wiki/Equatorial_Guinea_women%27s_national_football_team" title="Equatorial Guinea women's national football team">women's national team</a> qualified for the <a href="/wiki/2011_FIFA_Women%27s_World_Cup" title="2011 FIFA Women's World Cup">2011 World Cup</a> in Germany. </p>
      <p>In June 2016, Equatorial Guinea was chosen to host the <a href="/wiki/2019_African_Games" title="2019 African Games">12th African Games</a> in 2019. </p>
      <p>Equatorial Guinea is famous for the swimmers <a href="/wiki/Eric_Moussambani" title="Eric Moussambani">Eric Moussambani</a>, nicknamed "Eric the Eel",<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[128]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Paula_Barila_Bolopa" title="Paula Barila Bolopa">Paula Barila Bolopa</a>, "Paula the Crawler", who attended the <a href="/wiki/2000_Summer_Olympics" title="2000 Summer Olympics">2000 Summer Olympics</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[129]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Equatorial_Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Equatorial_Guinea&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="reflist columns references-column-width" style="column-width: 35em; list-style-type: lower-alpha;"> 
       <ol class="references"> 
        <li id="cite_note-11"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-11">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><small>Spanish:&nbsp;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Spanish" title="Help:IPA/Spanish">[giˈnea ekwatoˈɾjal]</a></span> <span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:Es-guinea_ecuatorial.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" decoding="async" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20"></a></span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/1/15/Es-guinea_ecuatorial.ogg" class="internal" title="Es-guinea ecuatorial.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</span></span> </li> 
        <li id="cite_note-12"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-12">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Local pronunciation: 
          <ul>
           <li>Spanish: <i lang="es">República de Guinea Ecuatorial</i> <small>Spanish pronunciation:&nbsp;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Spanish" title="Help:IPA/Spanish">[reˈpuβlika ðe ɣiˈnea ekwatoˈɾjal]</a></span> <span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:Es-republica_guinea_ecuatorial.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" decoding="async" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20"></a></span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/83/Es-republica_guinea_ecuatorial.ogg" class="internal" title="Es-republica guinea ecuatorial.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</span></li> 
           <li>French: <i lang="fr">République de Guinée équatoriale</i> <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/French" title="Help:IPA/French">[ʁepyblik d(ə) ɡine ekwatoˈʁjal]</a></span></li> 
           <li>Portuguese: <i lang="pt">República da Guiné Equatorial</i> <span style="font-size:85%;">Portuguese pronunciation:&nbsp;</span><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Portuguese" title="Help:IPA/Portuguese">[ʁɛˈpublikɐ dɐ giˈnɛ ˌekwɐtuɾiˈaɫ]</a></span></li>
          </ul> </span></li> 
       </ol>
